</blockquote>

<a name="speech3"><b>Chamberlain</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.13">Good day to both your graces.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech4"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.14">How is the king employ'd?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech5"><b>Chamberlain</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.15">I left him private,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.16">Full of sad thoughts and troubles.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech6"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.17">What's the cause?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech7"><b>Chamberlain</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.18">It seems the marriage with his brother's wife</a><br>
<a name="2.2.19">Has crept too near his conscience.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech8"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.20">No, his conscience</a><br>
<a name="2.2.21">Has crept too near another lady.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech9"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.22">'Tis so:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.23">This is the cardinal's doing, the king-cardinal:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.24">That blind priest, like the eldest son of fortune,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.25">Turns what he list. The king will know him one day.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech10"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.26">Pray God he do! he'll never know himself else.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech11"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.27">How holily he works in all his business!</a><br>
<a name="2.2.28">And with what zeal! for, now he has crack'd the league</a><br>
<a name="2.2.29">Between us and the emperor, the queen's great nephew,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.30">He dives into the king's soul, and there scatters</a><br>
<a name="2.2.31">Dangers, doubts, wringing of the conscience,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.32">Fears, and despairs; and all these for his marriage:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.33">And out of all these to restore the king,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.34">He counsels a divorce; a loss of her</a><br>
<a name="2.2.35">That, like a jewel, has hung twenty years</a><br>
<a name="2.2.36">About his neck, yet never lost her lustre;</a><br>
<a name="2.2.37">Of her that loves him with that excellence</a><br>
<a name="2.2.38">That angels love good men with; even of her</a><br>
<a name="2.2.39">That, when the greatest stroke of fortune falls,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.40">Will bless the king: and is not this course pious?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech12"><b>Chamberlain</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.41">Heaven keep me from such counsel! 'Tis most true</a><br>
<a name="2.2.42">These news are every where; every tongue speaks 'em,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.43">And every true heart weeps for't: all that dare</a><br>
<a name="2.2.44">Look into these affairs see this main end,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.45">The French king's sister. Heaven will one day open</a><br>
<a name="2.2.46">The king's eyes, that so long have slept upon</a><br>
<a name="2.2.47">This bold bad man.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech13"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.48">                  And free us from his slavery.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech14"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.49">We had need pray,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.50">And heartily, for our deliverance;</a><br>
<a name="2.2.51">Or this imperious man will work us all</a><br>
<a name="2.2.52">From princes into pages: all men's honours</a><br>
<a name="2.2.53">Lie like one lump before him, to be fashion'd</a><br>
<a name="2.2.54">Into what pitch he please.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech15"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.55">For me, my lords,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.56">I love him not, nor fear him; there's my creed:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.57">As I am made without him, so I'll stand,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.58">If the king please; his curses and his blessings</a><br>
<a name="2.2.59">Touch me alike, they're breath I not believe in.</a><br>
<a name="2.2.60">I knew him, and I know him; so I leave him</a><br>
<a name="2.2.61">To him that made him proud, the pope.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech16"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.62">Let's in;</a><br>
<a name="2.2.63">And with some other business put the king</a><br>
<a name="2.2.64">From these sad thoughts, that work too much upon him:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.65">My lord, you'll bear us company?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech17"><b>Chamberlain</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.66">Excuse me;</a><br>
<a name="2.2.67">The king has sent me otherwhere: besides,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.68">You'll find a most unfit time to disturb him:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.69">Health to your lordships.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech18"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.70">Thanks, my good lord chamberlain.</a><br>
<p><i>Exit Chamberlain; and KING HENRY VIII draws the curtain, and sits reading pensively</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech19"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.71">How sad he looks! sure, he is much afflicted.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech20"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.72">Who's there, ha?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech21"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.73">                  Pray God he be not angry.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech22"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.74">Who's there, I say? How dare you thrust yourselves</a><br>
<a name="2.2.75">Into my private meditations?</a><br>
<a name="2.2.76">Who am I? ha?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech23"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.77">A gracious king that pardons all offences</a><br>
<a name="2.2.78">Malice ne'er meant: our breach of duty this way</a><br>
<a name="2.2.79">Is business of estate; in which we come</a><br>
<a name="2.2.80">To know your royal pleasure.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech24"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.81">Ye are too bold:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.82">Go to; I'll make ye know your times of business:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.83">Is this an hour for temporal affairs, ha?</a><br>
<p><i>Enter CARDINAL WOLSEY and CARDINAL CAMPEIUS, with a commission</i></p>
<a name="2.2.84">Who's there? my good lord cardinal? O my Wolsey,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.85">The quiet of my wounded conscience;</a><br>
<a name="2.2.86">Thou art a cure fit for a king.</a><br>
<p><i>To CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</i></p>
<a name="2.2.87">You're welcome,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.88">Most learned reverend sir, into our kingdom:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.89">Use us and it.</a><br>
<p><i>To CARDINAL WOLSEY</i></p>
<a name="2.2.90">My good lord, have great care</a><br>
<a name="2.2.91">I be not found a talker.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech25"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.92">Sir, you cannot.</a><br>
<a name="2.2.93">I would your grace would give us but an hour</a><br>
<a name="2.2.94">Of private conference.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech26"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.95">[To NORFOLK and SUFFOLK]</a><br>
<a name="2.2.96">We are busy; go.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech27"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.97">[Aside to SUFFOLK]</a><br>
<a name="2.2.98">This priest has no pride in him?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech28"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.99">[Aside to NORFOLK]             Not to speak of:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.100">I would not be so sick though for his place:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.101">But this cannot continue.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech29"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.102">[Aside to SUFFOLK]      If it do,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.103">I'll venture one have-at-him.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech30"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.104">[Aside to NORFOLK]          I another.</a><br>
<p><i>Exeunt NORFOLK and SUFFOLK</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech31"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.105">Your grace has given a precedent of wisdom</a><br>
<a name="2.2.106">Above all princes, in committing freely</a><br>
<a name="2.2.107">Your scruple to the voice of Christendom:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.108">Who can be angry now? what envy reach you?</a><br>
<a name="2.2.109">The Spaniard, tied blood and favour to her,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.110">Must now confess, if they have any goodness,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.111">The trial just and noble. All the clerks,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.112">I mean the learned ones, in Christian kingdoms</a><br>
<a name="2.2.113">Have their free voices: Rome, the nurse of judgment,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.114">Invited by your noble self, hath sent</a><br>
<a name="2.2.115">One general tongue unto us, this good man,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.116">This just and learned priest, Cardinal Campeius;</a><br>
<a name="2.2.117">Whom once more I present unto your highness.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech32"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.118">And once more in mine arms I bid him welcome,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.119">And thank the holy conclave for their loves:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.120">They have sent me such a man I would have wish'd for.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech33"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.121">Your grace must needs deserve all strangers' loves,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.122">You are so noble. To your highness' hand</a><br>
<a name="2.2.123">I tender my commission; by whose virtue,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.124">The court of Rome commanding, you, my lord</a><br>
<a name="2.2.125">Cardinal of York, are join'd with me their servant</a><br>
<a name="2.2.126">In the unpartial judging of this business.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech34"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.127">Two equal men. The queen shall be acquainted</a><br>
<a name="2.2.128">Forthwith for what you come. Where's Gardiner?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech35"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.129">I know your majesty has always loved her</a><br>
<a name="2.2.130">So dear in heart, not to deny her that</a><br>
<a name="2.2.131">A woman of less place might ask by law:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.132">Scholars allow'd freely to argue for her.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech36"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.133">Ay, and the best she shall have; and my favour</a><br>
<a name="2.2.134">To him that does best: God forbid else. Cardinal,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.135">Prithee, call Gardiner to me, my new secretary:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.136">I find him a fit fellow.</a><br>
<p><i>Exit CARDINAL WOLSEY</i></p>
<p><i>Re-enter CARDINAL WOLSEY, with GARDINER</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech37"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.137">[Aside to GARDINER]  Give me your hand much joy and</a><br>
<a name="2.2.138">favour to you;</a><br>
<a name="2.2.139">You are the king's now.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech38"><b>GARDINER</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.140">[Aside to CARDINAL WOLSEY]</a><br>
<a name="2.2.141">But to be commanded</a><br>
<a name="2.2.142">For ever by your grace, whose hand has raised me.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech39"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.143">Come hither, Gardiner.</a><br>
<p><i>Walks and whispers</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech40"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.144">My Lord of York, was not one Doctor Pace</a><br>
<a name="2.2.145">In this man's place before him?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech41"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.146">Yes, he was.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech42"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.147">Was he not held a learned man?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech43"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.148">Yes, surely.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech44"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.149">Believe me, there's an ill opinion spread then</a><br>
<a name="2.2.150">Even of yourself, lord cardinal.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech45"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.151">How! of me?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech46"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.152">They will not stick to say you envied him,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.153">And fearing he would rise, he was so virtuous,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.154">Kept him a foreign man still; which so grieved him,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.155">That he ran mad and died.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech47"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.156">Heaven's peace be with him!</a><br>
<a name="2.2.157">That's Christian care enough: for living murmurers</a><br>
<a name="2.2.158">There's places of rebuke. He was a fool;</a><br>
<a name="2.2.159">For he would needs be virtuous: that good fellow,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.160">If I command him, follows my appointment:</a><br>
<a name="2.2.161">I will have none so near else. Learn this, brother,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.162">We live not to be grip'd by meaner persons.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech48"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.2.163">Deliver this with modesty to the queen.</a><br>
<p><i>Exit GARDINER</i></p>
<a name="2.2.164">The most convenient place that I can think of</a><br>
<a name="2.2.165">For such receipt of learning is Black-Friars;</a><br>
<a name="2.2.166">There ye shall meet about this weighty business.</a><br>
<a name="2.2.167">My Wolsey, see it furnish'd. O, my lord,</a><br>
<a name="2.2.168">Would it not grieve an able man to leave</a><br>
<a name="2.2.169">So sweet a bedfellow? But, conscience, conscience!</a><br>
<a name="2.2.170">O, 'tis a tender place; and I must leave her.</a><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. An ante-chamber of the QUEEN'S apartments.</h3>
<p></p><blockquote>
<i>Enter ANNE and an Old Lady</i>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech1"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.1">Not for that neither: here's the pang that pinches:</a><br>
<a name="2.3.2">His highness having lived so long with her, and she</a><br>
<a name="2.3.3">So good a lady that no tongue could ever</a><br>
<a name="2.3.4">Pronounce dishonour of her; by my life,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.5">She never knew harm-doing: O, now, after</a><br>
<a name="2.3.6">So many courses of the sun enthroned,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.7">Still growing in a majesty and pomp, the which</a><br>
<a name="2.3.8">To leave a thousand-fold more bitter than</a><br>
<a name="2.3.9">'Tis sweet at first to acquire,--after this process,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.10">To give her the avaunt! it is a pity</a><br>
<a name="2.3.11">Would move a monster.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech2"><b>Old Lady</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.12">Hearts of most hard temper</a><br>
<a name="2.3.13">Melt and lament for her.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech3"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.14">O, God's will! much better</a><br>
<a name="2.3.15">She ne'er had known pomp: though't be temporal,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.16">Yet, if that quarrel, fortune, do divorce</a><br>
<a name="2.3.17">It from the bearer, 'tis a sufferance panging</a><br>
<a name="2.3.18">As soul and body's severing.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech4"><b>Old Lady</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.19">Alas, poor lady!</a><br>
<a name="2.3.20">She's a stranger now again.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech5"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.21">So much the more</a><br>
<a name="2.3.22">Must pity drop upon her. Verily,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.23">I swear, 'tis better to be lowly born,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.24">And range with humble livers in content,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.25">Than to be perk'd up in a glistering grief,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.26">And wear a golden sorrow.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech6"><b>Old Lady</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.27">Our content</a><br>
<a name="2.3.28">Is our best having.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech7"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.29">By my troth and maidenhead,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.30">I would not be a queen.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech8"><b>Old Lady</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.31">Beshrew me, I would,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.32">And venture maidenhead for't; and so would you,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.33">For all this spice of your hypocrisy:</a><br>
<a name="2.3.34">You, that have so fair parts of woman on you,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.35">Have too a woman's heart; which ever yet</a><br>
<a name="2.3.36">Affected eminence, wealth, sovereignty;</a><br>
<a name="2.3.37">Which, to say sooth, are blessings; and which gifts,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.38">Saving your mincing, the capacity</a><br>
<a name="2.3.39">Of your soft cheveril conscience would receive,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.40">If you might please to stretch it.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech9"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.41">Nay, good troth.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech10"><b>Old Lady</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.42">Yes, troth, and troth; you would not be a queen?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech11"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.43">No, not for all the riches under heaven.</a><br>
<a name="2.3.44">Old Lady:	'Tis strange: a three-pence bow'd would hire me,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.45">Old as I am, to queen it: but, I pray you,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.46">What think you of a duchess? have you limbs</a><br>
<a name="2.3.47">To bear that load of title?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech12"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.48">No, in truth.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech13"><b>Old Lady</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.49">Then you are weakly made: pluck off a little;</a><br>
<a name="2.3.50">I would not be a young count in your way,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.51">For more than blushing comes to: if your back</a><br>
<a name="2.3.52">Cannot vouchsafe this burthen,'tis too weak</a><br>
<a name="2.3.53">Ever to get a boy.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech14"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.54">                  How you do talk!</a><br>
<a name="2.3.55">I swear again, I would not be a queen</a><br>
<a name="2.3.56">For all the world.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech15"><b>Old Lady</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.57">                  In faith, for little England</a><br>
<a name="2.3.58">You'ld venture an emballing: I myself</a><br>
<a name="2.3.59">Would for Carnarvonshire, although there long'd</a><br>
<a name="2.3.60">No more to the crown but that. Lo, who comes here?</a><br>
<p><i>Enter Chamberlain</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech16"><b>Chamberlain</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.61">Good morrow, ladies. What were't worth to know</a><br>
<a name="2.3.62">The secret of your conference?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech17"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.63">My good lord,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.64">Not your demand; it values not your asking:</a><br>
<a name="2.3.65">Our mistress' sorrows we were pitying.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech18"><b>Chamberlain</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.66">It was a gentle business, and becoming</a><br>
<a name="2.3.67">The action of good women: there is hope</a><br>
<a name="2.3.68">All will be well.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech19"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.69">                  Now, I pray God, amen!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech20"><b>Chamberlain</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.70">You bear a gentle mind, and heavenly blessings</a><br>
<a name="2.3.71">Follow such creatures. That you may, fair lady,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.72">Perceive I speak sincerely, and high note's</a><br>
<a name="2.3.73">Ta'en of your many virtues, the king's majesty</a><br>
<a name="2.3.74">Commends his good opinion of you, and</a><br>
<a name="2.3.75">Does purpose honour to you no less flowing</a><br>
<a name="2.3.76">Than Marchioness of Pembroke: to which title</a><br>
<a name="2.3.77">A thousand pound a year, annual support,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.78">Out of his grace he adds.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech21"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.79">I do not know</a><br>
<a name="2.3.80">What kind of my obedience I should tender;</a><br>
<a name="2.3.81">More than my all is nothing: nor my prayers</a><br>
<a name="2.3.82">Are not words duly hallow'd, nor my wishes</a><br>
<a name="2.3.83">More worth than empty vanities; yet prayers and wishes</a><br>
<a name="2.3.84">Are all I can return. Beseech your lordship,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.85">Vouchsafe to speak my thanks and my obedience,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.86">As from a blushing handmaid, to his highness;</a><br>
<a name="2.3.87">Whose health and royalty I pray for.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech22"><b>Chamberlain</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.88">Lady,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.89">I shall not fail to approve the fair conceit</a><br>
<a name="2.3.90">The king hath of you.</a><br>
<p><i>Aside</i></p>
<a name="2.3.91">I have perused her well;</a><br>
<a name="2.3.92">Beauty and honour in her are so mingled</a><br>
<a name="2.3.93">That they have caught the king: and who knows yet</a><br>
<a name="2.3.94">But from this lady may proceed a gem</a><br>
<a name="2.3.95">To lighten all this isle? I'll to the king,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.96">And say I spoke with you.</a><br>
<p><i>Exit Chamberlain</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech23"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.97">My honour'd lord.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech24"><b>Old Lady</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.98">Why, this it is; see, see!</a><br>
<a name="2.3.99">I have been begging sixteen years in court,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.100">Am yet a courtier beggarly, nor could</a><br>
<a name="2.3.101">Come pat betwixt too early and too late</a><br>
<a name="2.3.102">For any suit of pounds; and you, O fate!</a><br>
<a name="2.3.103">A very fresh-fish here--fie, fie, fie upon</a><br>
<a name="2.3.104">This compell'd fortune!--have your mouth fill'd up</a><br>
<a name="2.3.105">Before you open it.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech25"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.106">This is strange to me.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech26"><b>Old Lady</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.107">How tastes it? is it bitter? forty pence, no.</a><br>
<a name="2.3.108">There was a lady once, 'tis an old story,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.109">That would not be a queen, that would she not,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.110">For all the mud in Egypt: have you heard it?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech27"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.111">Come, you are pleasant.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech28"><b>Old Lady</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.112">With your theme, I could</a><br>
<a name="2.3.113">O'ermount the lark. The Marchioness of Pembroke!</a><br>
<a name="2.3.114">A thousand pounds a year for pure respect!</a><br>
<a name="2.3.115">No other obligation! By my life,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.116">That promises moe thousands: honour's train</a><br>
<a name="2.3.117">Is longer than his foreskirt. By this time</a><br>
<a name="2.3.118">I know your back will bear a duchess: say,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.119">Are you not stronger than you were?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech29"><b>ANNE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.120">Good lady,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.121">Make yourself mirth with your particular fancy,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.122">And leave me out on't. Would I had no being,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.123">If this salute my blood a jot: it faints me,</a><br>
<a name="2.3.124">To think what follows.</a><br>
<a name="2.3.125">The queen is comfortless, and we forgetful</a><br>
<a name="2.3.126">In our long absence: pray, do not deliver</a><br>
<a name="2.3.127">What here you've heard to her.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech30"><b>Old Lady</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.3.128">What do you think me?</a><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE IV. A hall in Black-Friars.</h3>
<p></p><blockquote>
<i>Trumpets, sennet, and cornets. Enter two Vergers,  with short silver wands; next them, two Scribes, in  the habit of doctors; after them, CANTERBURY alone;  after him, LINCOLN, Ely, Rochester, and Saint  Asaph; next them, with some small distance, follows  a Gentleman bearing the purse, with the great seal,  and a cardinal's hat; then two Priests, bearing  each a silver cross; then a Gentleman-usher  bare-headed, accompanied with a Sergeant-at-arms  bearing a silver mace; then two Gentlemen bearing  two great silver pillars; after them, side by side,  CARDINAL WOLSEY and CARDINAL CAMPEIUS; two Noblemen  with the sword and mace. KING HENRY VIII takes  place under the cloth of state; CARDINAL WOLSEY and  CARDINAL CAMPEIUS sit under him as judges. QUEEN  KATHARINE takes place some distance from KING  HENRY VIII. The Bishops place themselves on each  side the court, in manner of a consistory; below  them, the Scribes. The Lords sit next the Bishops.  The rest of the Attendants stand in convenient order about the stage</i>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech1"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.1">Whilst our commission from Rome is read,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.2">Let silence be commanded.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech2"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.3">What's the need?</a><br>
<a name="2.4.4">It hath already publicly been read,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.5">And on all sides the authority allow'd;</a><br>
<a name="2.4.6">You may, then, spare that time.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech3"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.7">Be't so. Proceed.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech4"><b>Scribe</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.8">Say, Henry King of England, come into the court.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech5"><b>Crier</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.9">Henry King of England,  &amp; c.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech6"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.10">Here.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech7"><b>Scribe</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.11">Say, Katharine Queen of England, come into the court.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech8"><b>Crier</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.12">Katharine Queen of England,  &amp; c.</a><br>
<p><i>QUEEN KATHARINE makes no answer, rises out of her  chair, goes about the court, comes to KING HENRY VIII, and kneels at his feet; then speaks</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech9"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.13">Sir, I desire you do me right and justice;</a><br>
<a name="2.4.14">And to bestow your pity on me: for</a><br>
<a name="2.4.15">I am a most poor woman, and a stranger,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.16">Born out of your dominions; having here</a><br>
<a name="2.4.17">No judge indifferent, nor no more assurance</a><br>
<a name="2.4.18">Of equal friendship and proceeding. Alas, sir,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.19">In what have I offended you? what cause</a><br>
<a name="2.4.20">Hath my behavior given to your displeasure,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.21">That thus you should proceed to put me off,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.22">And take your good grace from me? Heaven witness,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.23">I have been to you a true and humble wife,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.24">At all times to your will conformable;</a><br>
<a name="2.4.25">Ever in fear to kindle your dislike,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.26">Yea, subject to your countenance, glad or sorry</a><br>
<a name="2.4.27">As I saw it inclined: when was the hour</a><br>
<a name="2.4.28">I ever contradicted your desire,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.29">Or made it not mine too? Or which of your friends</a><br>
<a name="2.4.30">Have I not strove to love, although I knew</a><br>
<a name="2.4.31">He were mine enemy? what friend of mine</a><br>
<a name="2.4.32">That had to him derived your anger, did I</a><br>
<a name="2.4.33">Continue in my liking? nay, gave notice</a><br>
<a name="2.4.34">He was from thence discharged. Sir, call to mind</a><br>
<a name="2.4.35">That I have been your wife, in this obedience,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.36">Upward of twenty years, and have been blest</a><br>
<a name="2.4.37">With many children by you: if, in the course</a><br>
<a name="2.4.38">And process of this time, you can report,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.39">And prove it too, against mine honour aught,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.40">My bond to wedlock, or my love and duty,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.41">Against your sacred person, in God's name,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.42">Turn me away; and let the foul'st contempt</a><br>
<a name="2.4.43">Shut door upon me, and so give me up</a><br>
<a name="2.4.44">To the sharp'st kind of justice. Please you sir,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.45">The king, your father, was reputed for</a><br>
<a name="2.4.46">A prince most prudent, of an excellent</a><br>
<a name="2.4.47">And unmatch'd wit and judgment: Ferdinand,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.48">My father, king of Spain, was reckon'd one</a><br>
<a name="2.4.49">The wisest prince that there had reign'd by many</a><br>
<a name="2.4.50">A year before: it is not to be question'd</a><br>
<a name="2.4.51">That they had gather'd a wise council to them</a><br>
<a name="2.4.52">Of every realm, that did debate this business,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.53">Who deem'd our marriage lawful: wherefore I humbly</a><br>
<a name="2.4.54">Beseech you, sir, to spare me, till I may</a><br>
<a name="2.4.55">Be by my friends in Spain advised; whose counsel</a><br>
<a name="2.4.56">I will implore: if not, i' the name of God,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.57">Your pleasure be fulfill'd!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech10"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.58">You have here, lady,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.59">And of your choice, these reverend fathers; men</a><br>
<a name="2.4.60">Of singular integrity and learning,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.61">Yea, the elect o' the land, who are assembled</a><br>
<a name="2.4.62">To plead your cause: it shall be therefore bootless</a><br>
<a name="2.4.63">That longer you desire the court; as well</a><br>
<a name="2.4.64">For your own quiet, as to rectify</a><br>
<a name="2.4.65">What is unsettled in the king.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech11"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.66">His grace</a><br>
<a name="2.4.67">Hath spoken well and justly: therefore, madam,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.68">It's fit this royal session do proceed;</a><br>
<a name="2.4.69">And that, without delay, their arguments</a><br>
<a name="2.4.70">Be now produced and heard.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech12"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.71">Lord cardinal,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.72">To you I speak.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech13"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.73">                  Your pleasure, madam?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech14"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.74">Sir,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.75">I am about to weep; but, thinking that</a><br>
<a name="2.4.76">We are a queen, or long have dream'd so, certain</a><br>
<a name="2.4.77">The daughter of a king, my drops of tears</a><br>
<a name="2.4.78">I'll turn to sparks of fire.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech15"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.79">Be patient yet.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech16"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.80">I will, when you are humble; nay, before,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.81">Or God will punish me. I do believe,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.82">Induced by potent circumstances, that</a><br>
<a name="2.4.83">You are mine enemy, and make my challenge</a><br>
<a name="2.4.84">You shall not be my judge: for it is you</a><br>
<a name="2.4.85">Have blown this coal betwixt my lord and me;</a><br>
<a name="2.4.86">Which God's dew quench! Therefore I say again,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.87">I utterly abhor, yea, from my soul</a><br>
<a name="2.4.88">Refuse you for my judge; whom, yet once more,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.89">I hold my most malicious foe, and think not</a><br>
<a name="2.4.90">At all a friend to truth.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech17"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.91">I do profess</a><br>
<a name="2.4.92">You speak not like yourself; who ever yet</a><br>
<a name="2.4.93">Have stood to charity, and display'd the effects</a><br>
<a name="2.4.94">Of disposition gentle, and of wisdom</a><br>
<a name="2.4.95">O'ertopping woman's power. Madam, you do me wrong:</a><br>
<a name="2.4.96">I have no spleen against you; nor injustice</a><br>
<a name="2.4.97">For you or any: how far I have proceeded,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.98">Or how far further shall, is warranted</a><br>
<a name="2.4.99">By a commission from the consistory,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.100">Yea, the whole consistory of Rome. You charge me</a><br>
<a name="2.4.101">That I have blown this coal: I do deny it:</a><br>
<a name="2.4.102">The king is present: if it be known to him</a><br>
<a name="2.4.103">That I gainsay my deed, how may he wound,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.104">And worthily, my falsehood! yea, as much</a><br>
<a name="2.4.105">As you have done my truth. If he know</a><br>
<a name="2.4.106">That I am free of your report, he knows</a><br>
<a name="2.4.107">I am not of your wrong. Therefore in him</a><br>
<a name="2.4.108">It lies to cure me: and the cure is, to</a><br>
<a name="2.4.109">Remove these thoughts from you: the which before</a><br>
<a name="2.4.110">His highness shall speak in, I do beseech</a><br>
<a name="2.4.111">You, gracious madam, to unthink your speaking</a><br>
<a name="2.4.112">And to say so no more.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech18"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.113">My lord, my lord,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.114">I am a simple woman, much too weak</a><br>
<a name="2.4.115">To oppose your cunning. You're meek and</a><br>
<a name="2.4.116">humble-mouth'd;</a><br>
<a name="2.4.117">You sign your place and calling, in full seeming,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.118">With meekness and humility; but your heart</a><br>
<a name="2.4.119">Is cramm'd with arrogancy, spleen, and pride.</a><br>
<a name="2.4.120">You have, by fortune and his highness' favours,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.121">Gone slightly o'er low steps and now are mounted</a><br>
<a name="2.4.122">Where powers are your retainers, and your words,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.123">Domestics to you, serve your will as't please</a><br>
<a name="2.4.124">Yourself pronounce their office. I must tell you,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.125">You tender more your person's honour than</a><br>
<a name="2.4.126">Your high profession spiritual: that again</a><br>
<a name="2.4.127">I do refuse you for my judge; and here,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.128">Before you all, appeal unto the pope,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.129">To bring my whole cause 'fore his holiness,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.130">And to be judged by him.</a><br>
<p><i>She curtsies to KING HENRY VIII, and offers to depart</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech19"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.131">The queen is obstinate,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.132">Stubborn to justice, apt to accuse it, and</a><br>
<a name="2.4.133">Disdainful to be tried by't: 'tis not well.</a><br>
<a name="2.4.134">She's going away.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech20"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.135">Call her again.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech21"><b>Crier</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.136">Katharine Queen of England, come into the court.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech22"><b>GRIFFITH</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.137">Madam, you are call'd back.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech23"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.138">What need you note it? pray you, keep your way:</a><br>
<a name="2.4.139">When you are call'd, return. Now, the Lord help,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.140">They vex me past my patience! Pray you, pass on:</a><br>
<a name="2.4.141">I will not tarry; no, nor ever more</a><br>
<a name="2.4.142">Upon this business my appearance make</a><br>
<a name="2.4.143">In any of their courts.</a><br>
<p><i>Exeunt QUEEN KATHARINE and her Attendants</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech24"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.144">Go thy ways, Kate:</a><br>
<a name="2.4.145">That man i' the world who shall report he has</a><br>
<a name="2.4.146">A better wife, let him in nought be trusted,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.147">For speaking false in that: thou art, alone,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.148">If thy rare qualities, sweet gentleness,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.149">Thy meekness saint-like, wife-like government,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.150">Obeying in commanding, and thy parts</a><br>
<a name="2.4.151">Sovereign and pious else, could speak thee out,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.152">The queen of earthly queens: she's noble born;</a><br>
<a name="2.4.153">And, like her true nobility, she has</a><br>
<a name="2.4.154">Carried herself towards me.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech25"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.155">Most gracious sir,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.156">In humblest manner I require your highness,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.157">That it shall please you to declare, in hearing</a><br>
<a name="2.4.158">Of all these ears,--for where I am robb'd and bound,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.159">There must I be unloosed, although not there</a><br>
<a name="2.4.160">At once and fully satisfied,--whether ever I</a><br>
<a name="2.4.161">Did broach this business to your highness; or</a><br>
<a name="2.4.162">Laid any scruple in your way, which might</a><br>
<a name="2.4.163">Induce you to the question on't? or ever</a><br>
<a name="2.4.164">Have to you, but with thanks to God for such</a><br>
<a name="2.4.165">A royal lady, spake one the least word that might</a><br>
<a name="2.4.166">Be to the prejudice of her present state,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.167">Or touch of her good person?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech26"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.168">My lord cardinal,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.169">I do excuse you; yea, upon mine honour,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.170">I free you from't. You are not to be taught</a><br>
<a name="2.4.171">That you have many enemies, that know not</a><br>
<a name="2.4.172">Why they are so, but, like to village-curs,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.173">Bark when their fellows do: by some of these</a><br>
<a name="2.4.174">The queen is put in anger. You're excused:</a><br>
<a name="2.4.175">But will you be more justified? You ever</a><br>
<a name="2.4.176">Have wish'd the sleeping of this business; never desired</a><br>
<a name="2.4.177">It to be stirr'd; but oft have hinder'd, oft,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.178">The passages made toward it: on my honour,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.179">I speak my good lord cardinal to this point,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.180">And thus far clear him. Now, what moved me to't,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.181">I will be bold with time and your attention:</a><br>
<a name="2.4.182">Then mark the inducement. Thus it came; give heed to't:</a><br>
<a name="2.4.183">My conscience first received a tenderness,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.184">Scruple, and prick, on certain speeches utter'd</a><br>
<a name="2.4.185">By the Bishop of Bayonne, then French ambassador;</a><br>
<a name="2.4.186">Who had been hither sent on the debating</a><br>
<a name="2.4.187">A marriage 'twixt the Duke of Orleans and</a><br>
<a name="2.4.188">Our daughter Mary: i' the progress of this business,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.189">Ere a determinate resolution, he,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.190">I mean the bishop, did require a respite;</a><br>
<a name="2.4.191">Wherein he might the king his lord advertise</a><br>
<a name="2.4.192">Whether our daughter were legitimate,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.193">Respecting this our marriage with the dowager,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.194">Sometimes our brother's wife. This respite shook</a><br>
<a name="2.4.195">The bosom of my conscience, enter'd me,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.196">Yea, with a splitting power, and made to tremble</a><br>
<a name="2.4.197">The region of my breast; which forced such way,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.198">That many mazed considerings did throng</a><br>
<a name="2.4.199">And press'd in with this caution. First, methought</a><br>
<a name="2.4.200">I stood not in the smile of heaven; who had</a><br>
<a name="2.4.201">Commanded nature, that my lady's womb,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.202">If it conceived a male child by me, should</a><br>
<a name="2.4.203">Do no more offices of life to't than</a><br>
<a name="2.4.204">The grave does to the dead; for her male issue</a><br>
<a name="2.4.205">Or died where they were made, or shortly after</a><br>
<a name="2.4.206">This world had air'd them: hence I took a thought,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.207">This was a judgment on me; that my kingdom,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.208">Well worthy the best heir o' the world, should not</a><br>
<a name="2.4.209">Be gladded in't by me: then follows, that</a><br>
<a name="2.4.210">I weigh'd the danger which my realms stood in</a><br>
<a name="2.4.211">By this my issue's fail; and that gave to me</a><br>
<a name="2.4.212">Many a groaning throe. Thus hulling in</a><br>
<a name="2.4.213">The wild sea of my conscience, I did steer</a><br>
<a name="2.4.214">Toward this remedy, whereupon we are</a><br>
<a name="2.4.215">Now present here together: that's to say,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.216">I meant to rectify my conscience,--which</a><br>
<a name="2.4.217">I then did feel full sick, and yet not well,--</a><br>
<a name="2.4.218">By all the reverend fathers of the land</a><br>
<a name="2.4.219">And doctors learn'd: first I began in private</a><br>
<a name="2.4.220">With you, my Lord of Lincoln; you remember</a><br>
<a name="2.4.221">How under my oppression I did reek,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.222">When I first moved you.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech27"><b>LINCOLN</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.223">Very well, my liege.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech28"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.224">I have spoke long: be pleased yourself to say</a><br>
<a name="2.4.225">How far you satisfied me.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech29"><b>LINCOLN</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.226">So please your highness,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.227">The question did at first so stagger me,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.228">Bearing a state of mighty moment in't</a><br>
<a name="2.4.229">And consequence of dread, that I committed</a><br>
<a name="2.4.230">The daring'st counsel which I had to doubt;</a><br>
<a name="2.4.231">And did entreat your highness to this course</a><br>
<a name="2.4.232">Which you are running here.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech30"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.233">I then moved you,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.234">My Lord of Canterbury; and got your leave</a><br>
<a name="2.4.235">To make this present summons: unsolicited</a><br>
<a name="2.4.236">I left no reverend person in this court;</a><br>
<a name="2.4.237">But by particular consent proceeded</a><br>
<a name="2.4.238">Under your hands and seals: therefore, go on:</a><br>
<a name="2.4.239">For no dislike i' the world against the person</a><br>
<a name="2.4.240">Of the good queen, but the sharp thorny points</a><br>
<a name="2.4.241">Of my alleged reasons, drive this forward:</a><br>
<a name="2.4.242">Prove but our marriage lawful, by my life</a><br>
<a name="2.4.243">And kingly dignity, we are contented</a><br>
<a name="2.4.244">To wear our mortal state to come with her,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.245">Katharine our queen, before the primest creature</a><br>
<a name="2.4.246">That's paragon'd o' the world.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech31"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.247">So please your highness,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.248">The queen being absent, 'tis a needful fitness</a><br>
<a name="2.4.249">That we adjourn this court till further day:</a><br>
<a name="2.4.250">Meanwhile must be an earnest motion</a><br>
<a name="2.4.251">Made to the queen, to call back her appeal</a><br>
<a name="2.4.252">She intends unto his holiness.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech32"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="2.4.253">[Aside]	I may perceive</a><br>
<a name="2.4.254">These cardinals trifle with me: I abhor</a><br>
<a name="2.4.255">This dilatory sloth and tricks of Rome.</a><br>
<a name="2.4.256">My learn'd and well-beloved servant, Cranmer,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.257">Prithee, return: with thy approach, I know,</a><br>
<a name="2.4.258">My comfort comes along. Break up the court:</a><br>
<a name="2.4.259">I say, set on.</a><br>
<p><i>Exeunt in manner as they entered</i></p>
</blockquote><p>
</p><h3>ACT III</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. London. QUEEN KATHARINE's apartments.</h3>
<p></p><blockquote>
<i>Enter QUEEN KATHARINE and her Women, as at work</i>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech1"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.1">Take thy lute, wench: my soul grows sad with troubles;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.2">Sing, and disperse 'em, if thou canst: leave working.</a><br>
<p><i>SONG</i></p>
<a name="3.1.3">Orpheus with his lute made trees,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.4">And the mountain tops that freeze,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.5">Bow themselves when he did sing:</a><br>
<a name="3.1.6">To his music plants and flowers</a><br>
<a name="3.1.7">Ever sprung; as sun and showers</a><br>
<a name="3.1.8">There had made a lasting spring.</a><br>
<a name="3.1.9">Every thing that heard him play,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.10">Even the billows of the sea,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.11">Hung their heads, and then lay by.</a><br>
<a name="3.1.12">In sweet music is such art,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.13">Killing care and grief of heart</a><br>
<a name="3.1.14">Fall asleep, or hearing, die.</a><br>
<p><i>Enter a Gentleman</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech2"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.15">How now!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech3"><b>Gentleman</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.16">An't please your grace, the two great cardinals</a><br>
<a name="3.1.17">Wait in the presence.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech4"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.18">Would they speak with me?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech5"><b>Gentleman</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.19">They will'd me say so, madam.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech6"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.20">Pray their graces</a><br>
<a name="3.1.21">To come near.</a><br>
<p><i>Exit Gentleman</i></p>
<a name="3.1.22">What can be their business</a><br>
<a name="3.1.23">With me, a poor weak woman, fall'n from favour?</a><br>
<a name="3.1.24">I do not like their coming. Now I think on't,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.25">They should be good men; their affairs as righteous:</a><br>
<a name="3.1.26">But all hoods make not monks.</a><br>
<p><i>Enter CARDINAL WOLSEY and CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech7"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.27">Peace to your highness!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech8"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.28">Your graces find me here part of a housewife,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.29">I would be all, against the worst may happen.</a><br>
<a name="3.1.30">What are your pleasures with me, reverend lords?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech9"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.31">May it please you noble madam, to withdraw</a><br>
<a name="3.1.32">Into your private chamber, we shall give you</a><br>
<a name="3.1.33">The full cause of our coming.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech10"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.34">Speak it here:</a><br>
<a name="3.1.35">There's nothing I have done yet, o' my conscience,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.36">Deserves a corner: would all other women</a><br>
<a name="3.1.37">Could speak this with as free a soul as I do!</a><br>
<a name="3.1.38">My lords, I care not, so much I am happy</a><br>
<a name="3.1.39">Above a number, if my actions</a><br>
<a name="3.1.40">Were tried by every tongue, every eye saw 'em,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.41">Envy and base opinion set against 'em,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.42">I know my life so even. If your business</a><br>
<a name="3.1.43">Seek me out, and that way I am wife in,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.44">Out with it boldly: truth loves open dealing.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech11"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.45">Tanta est erga te mentis integritas, regina</a><br>
<a name="3.1.46">serenissima,--</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech12"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.47">O, good my lord, no Latin;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.48">I am not such a truant since my coming,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.49">As not to know the language I have lived in:</a><br>
<a name="3.1.50">A strange tongue makes my cause more strange,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.51">suspicious;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.52">Pray, speak in English: here are some will thank you,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.53">If you speak truth, for their poor mistress' sake;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.54">Believe me, she has had much wrong: lord cardinal,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.55">The willing'st sin I ever yet committed</a><br>
<a name="3.1.56">May be absolved in English.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech13"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.57">Noble lady,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.58">I am sorry my integrity should breed,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.59">And service to his majesty and you,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.60">So deep suspicion, where all faith was meant.</a><br>
<a name="3.1.61">We come not by the way of accusation,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.62">To taint that honour every good tongue blesses,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.63">Nor to betray you any way to sorrow,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.64">You have too much, good lady; but to know</a><br>
<a name="3.1.65">How you stand minded in the weighty difference</a><br>
<a name="3.1.66">Between the king and you; and to deliver,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.67">Like free and honest men, our just opinions</a><br>
<a name="3.1.68">And comforts to your cause.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech14"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.69">Most honour'd madam,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.70">My Lord of York, out of his noble nature,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.71">Zeal and obedience he still bore your grace,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.72">Forgetting, like a good man your late censure</a><br>
<a name="3.1.73">Both of his truth and him, which was too far,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.74">Offers, as I do, in a sign of peace,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.75">His service and his counsel.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech15"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.76">[Aside]	To betray me.--</a><br>
<a name="3.1.77">My lords, I thank you both for your good wills;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.78">Ye speak like honest men; pray God, ye prove so!</a><br>
<a name="3.1.79">But how to make ye suddenly an answer,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.80">In such a point of weight, so near mine honour,--</a><br>
<a name="3.1.81">More near my life, I fear,--with my weak wit,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.82">And to such men of gravity and learning,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.83">In truth, I know not. I was set at work</a><br>
<a name="3.1.84">Among my maids: full little, God knows, looking</a><br>
<a name="3.1.85">Either for such men or such business.</a><br>
<a name="3.1.86">For her sake that I have been,--for I feel</a><br>
<a name="3.1.87">The last fit of my greatness,--good your graces,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.88">Let me have time and counsel for my cause:</a><br>
<a name="3.1.89">Alas, I am a woman, friendless, hopeless!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech16"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.90">Madam, you wrong the king's love with these fears:</a><br>
<a name="3.1.91">Your hopes and friends are infinite.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech17"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.92">In England</a><br>
<a name="3.1.93">But little for my profit: can you think, lords,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.94">That any Englishman dare give me counsel?</a><br>
<a name="3.1.95">Or be a known friend, 'gainst his highness' pleasure,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.96">Though he be grown so desperate to be honest,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.97">And live a subject? Nay, forsooth, my friends,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.98">They that must weigh out my afflictions,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.99">They that my trust must grow to, live not here:</a><br>
<a name="3.1.100">They are, as all my other comforts, far hence</a><br>
<a name="3.1.101">In mine own country, lords.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech18"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.102">I would your grace</a><br>
<a name="3.1.103">Would leave your griefs, and take my counsel.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech19"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.104">How, sir?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech20"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.105">Put your main cause into the king's protection;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.106">He's loving and most gracious: 'twill be much</a><br>
<a name="3.1.107">Both for your honour better and your cause;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.108">For if the trial of the law o'ertake ye,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.109">You'll part away disgraced.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech21"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.110">He tells you rightly.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech22"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.111">Ye tell me what ye wish for both,--my ruin:</a><br>
<a name="3.1.112">Is this your Christian counsel? out upon ye!</a><br>
<a name="3.1.113">Heaven is above all yet; there sits a judge</a><br>
<a name="3.1.114">That no king can corrupt.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech23"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.115">Your rage mistakes us.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech24"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.116">The more shame for ye: holy men I thought ye,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.117">Upon my soul, two reverend cardinal virtues;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.118">But cardinal sins and hollow hearts I fear ye:</a><br>
<a name="3.1.119">Mend 'em, for shame, my lords. Is this your comfort?</a><br>
<a name="3.1.120">The cordial that ye bring a wretched lady,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.121">A woman lost among ye, laugh'd at, scorn'd?</a><br>
<a name="3.1.122">I will not wish ye half my miseries;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.123">I have more charity: but say, I warn'd ye;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.124">Take heed, for heaven's sake, take heed, lest at once</a><br>
<a name="3.1.125">The burthen of my sorrows fall upon ye.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech25"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.126">Madam, this is a mere distraction;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.127">You turn the good we offer into envy.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech26"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.128">Ye turn me into nothing: woe upon ye</a><br>
<a name="3.1.129">And all such false professors! would you have me--</a><br>
<a name="3.1.130">If you have any justice, any pity;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.131">If ye be any thing but churchmen's habits--</a><br>
<a name="3.1.132">Put my sick cause into his hands that hates me?</a><br>
<a name="3.1.133">Alas, has banish'd me his bed already,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.134">His love, too long ago! I am old, my lords,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.135">And all the fellowship I hold now with him</a><br>
<a name="3.1.136">Is only my obedience. What can happen</a><br>
<a name="3.1.137">To me above this wretchedness? all your studies</a><br>
<a name="3.1.138">Make me a curse like this.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech27"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.139">Your fears are worse.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech28"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.140">Have I lived thus long--let me speak myself,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.141">Since virtue finds no friends--a wife, a true one?</a><br>
<a name="3.1.142">A woman, I dare say without vain-glory,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.143">Never yet branded with suspicion?</a><br>
<a name="3.1.144">Have I with all my full affections</a><br>
<a name="3.1.145">Still met the king? loved him next heaven?</a><br>
<a name="3.1.146">obey'd him?</a><br>
<a name="3.1.147">Been, out of fondness, superstitious to him?</a><br>
<a name="3.1.148">Almost forgot my prayers to content him?</a><br>
<a name="3.1.149">And am I thus rewarded? 'tis not well, lords.</a><br>
<a name="3.1.150">Bring me a constant woman to her husband,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.151">One that ne'er dream'd a joy beyond his pleasure;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.152">And to that woman, when she has done most,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.153">Yet will I add an honour, a great patience.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech29"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.154">Madam, you wander from the good we aim at.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech30"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.155">My lord, I dare not make myself so guilty,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.156">To give up willingly that noble title</a><br>
<a name="3.1.157">Your master wed me to: nothing but death</a><br>
<a name="3.1.158">Shall e'er divorce my dignities.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech31"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.159">Pray, hear me.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech32"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.160">Would I had never trod this English earth,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.161">Or felt the flatteries that grow upon it!</a><br>
<a name="3.1.162">Ye have angels' faces, but heaven knows your hearts.</a><br>
<a name="3.1.163">What will become of me now, wretched lady!</a><br>
<a name="3.1.164">I am the most unhappy woman living.</a><br>
<a name="3.1.165">Alas, poor wenches, where are now your fortunes!</a><br>
<a name="3.1.166">Shipwreck'd upon a kingdom, where no pity,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.167">No friend, no hope; no kindred weep for me;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.168">Almost no grave allow'd me: like the lily,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.169">That once was mistress of the field and flourish'd,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.170">I'll hang my head and perish.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech33"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.171">If your grace</a><br>
<a name="3.1.172">Could but be brought to know our ends are honest,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.173">You'ld feel more comfort: why should we, good lady,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.174">Upon what cause, wrong you? alas, our places,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.175">The way of our profession is against it:</a><br>
<a name="3.1.176">We are to cure such sorrows, not to sow 'em.</a><br>
<a name="3.1.177">For goodness' sake, consider what you do;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.178">How you may hurt yourself, ay, utterly</a><br>
<a name="3.1.179">Grow from the king's acquaintance, by this carriage.</a><br>
<a name="3.1.180">The hearts of princes kiss obedience,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.181">So much they love it; but to stubborn spirits</a><br>
<a name="3.1.182">They swell, and grow as terrible as storms.</a><br>
<a name="3.1.183">I know you have a gentle, noble temper,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.184">A soul as even as a calm: pray, think us</a><br>
<a name="3.1.185">Those we profess, peace-makers, friends, and servants.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech34"><b>CARDINAL CAMPEIUS</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.186">Madam, you'll find it so. You wrong your virtues</a><br>
<a name="3.1.187">With these weak women's fears: a noble spirit,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.188">As yours was put into you, ever casts</a><br>
<a name="3.1.189">Such doubts, as false coin, from it. The king loves you;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.190">Beware you lose it not: for us, if you please</a><br>
<a name="3.1.191">To trust us in your business, we are ready</a><br>
<a name="3.1.192">To use our utmost  studies in your service.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech35"><b>QUEEN KATHARINE</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.1.193">Do what ye will, my lords: and, pray, forgive me,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.194">If I have used myself unmannerly;</a><br>
<a name="3.1.195">You know I am a woman, lacking wit</a><br>
<a name="3.1.196">To make a seemly answer to such persons.</a><br>
<a name="3.1.197">Pray, do my service to his majesty:</a><br>
<a name="3.1.198">He has my heart yet; and shall have my prayers</a><br>
<a name="3.1.199">While I shall have my life. Come, reverend fathers,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.200">Bestow your counsels on me: she now begs,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.201">That little thought, when she set footing here,</a><br>
<a name="3.1.202">She should have bought her dignities so dear.</a><br>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. Ante-chamber to KING HENRY VIII's apartment.</h3>
<p></p><blockquote>
<i>Enter NORFOLK, SUFFOLK, SURREY, and Chamberlain</i>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech1"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.1">If you will now unite in your complaints,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.2">And force them with a constancy, the cardinal</a><br>
<a name="3.2.3">Cannot stand under them: if you omit</a><br>
<a name="3.2.4">The offer of this time, I cannot promise</a><br>
<a name="3.2.5">But that you shall sustain moe new disgraces,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.6">With these you bear already.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech2"><b>SURREY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.7">I am joyful</a><br>
<a name="3.2.8">To meet the least occasion that may give me</a><br>
<a name="3.2.9">Remembrance of my father-in-law, the duke,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.10">To be revenged on him.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech3"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.11">Which of the peers</a><br>
<a name="3.2.12">Have uncontemn'd gone by him, or at least</a><br>
<a name="3.2.13">Strangely neglected? when did he regard</a><br>
<a name="3.2.14">The stamp of nobleness in any person</a><br>
<a name="3.2.15">Out of himself?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech4"><b>Chamberlain</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.16">                  My lords, you speak your pleasures:</a><br>
<a name="3.2.17">What he deserves of you and me I know;</a><br>
<a name="3.2.18">What we can do to him, though now the time</a><br>
<a name="3.2.19">Gives way to us, I much fear. If you cannot</a><br>
<a name="3.2.20">Bar his access to the king, never attempt</a><br>
<a name="3.2.21">Any thing on him; for he hath a witchcraft</a><br>
<a name="3.2.22">Over the king in's tongue.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech5"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.23">O, fear him not;</a><br>
<a name="3.2.24">His spell in that is out: the king hath found</a><br>
<a name="3.2.25">Matter against him that for ever mars</a><br>
<a name="3.2.26">The honey of his language. No, he's settled,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.27">Not to come off, in his displeasure.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech6"><b>SURREY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.28">Sir,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.29">I should be glad to hear such news as this</a><br>
<a name="3.2.30">Once every hour.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech7"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.31">                  Believe it, this is true:</a><br>
<a name="3.2.32">In the divorce his contrary proceedings</a><br>
<a name="3.2.33">Are all unfolded wherein he appears</a><br>
<a name="3.2.34">As I would wish mine enemy.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech8"><b>SURREY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.35">How came</a><br>
<a name="3.2.36">His practises to light?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech9"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.37">Most strangely.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech10"><b>SURREY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.38">O, how, how?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech11"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.39">The cardinal's letters to the pope miscarried,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.40">And came to the eye o' the king: wherein was read,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.41">How that the cardinal did entreat his holiness</a><br>
<a name="3.2.42">To stay the judgment o' the divorce; for if</a><br>
<a name="3.2.43">It did take place, 'I do,' quoth he, 'perceive</a><br>
<a name="3.2.44">My king is tangled in affection to</a><br>
<a name="3.2.45">A creature of the queen's, Lady Anne Bullen.'</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech12"><b>SURREY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.46">Has the king this?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech13"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.47">                  Believe it.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech14"><b>SURREY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.48">Will this work?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech15"><b>Chamberlain</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.49">The king in this perceives him, how he coasts</a><br>
<a name="3.2.50">And hedges his own way. But in this point</a><br>
<a name="3.2.51">All his tricks founder, and he brings his physic</a><br>
<a name="3.2.52">After his patient's death: the king already</a><br>
<a name="3.2.53">Hath married the fair lady.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech16"><b>SURREY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.54">Would he had!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech17"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.55">May you be happy in your wish, my lord</a><br>
<a name="3.2.56">For, I profess, you have it.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech18"><b>SURREY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.57">Now, all my joy</a><br>
<a name="3.2.58">Trace the conjunction!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech19"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.59">My amen to't!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech20"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.60">All men's!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech21"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.61">There's order given for her coronation:</a><br>
<a name="3.2.62">Marry, this is yet but young, and may be left</a><br>
<a name="3.2.63">To some ears unrecounted. But, my lords,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.64">She is a gallant creature, and complete</a><br>
<a name="3.2.65">In mind and feature: I persuade me, from her</a><br>
<a name="3.2.66">Will fall some blessing to this land, which shall</a><br>
<a name="3.2.67">In it be memorised.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech22"><b>SURREY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.68">But, will the king</a><br>
<a name="3.2.69">Digest this letter of the cardinal's?</a><br>
<a name="3.2.70">The Lord forbid!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech23"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.71">                  Marry, amen!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech24"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.72">No, no;</a><br>
<a name="3.2.73">There be moe wasps that buzz about his nose</a><br>
<a name="3.2.74">Will make this sting the sooner. Cardinal Campeius</a><br>
<a name="3.2.75">Is stol'n away to Rome; hath ta'en no leave;</a><br>
<a name="3.2.76">Has left the cause o' the king unhandled; and</a><br>
<a name="3.2.77">Is posted, as the agent of our cardinal,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.78">To second all his plot. I do assure you</a><br>
<a name="3.2.79">The king cried Ha! at this.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech25"><b>Chamberlain</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.80">Now, God incense him,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.81">And let him cry Ha! louder!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech26"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.82">But, my lord,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.83">When returns Cranmer?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech27"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.84">He is return'd in his opinions; which</a><br>
<a name="3.2.85">Have satisfied the king for his divorce,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.86">Together with all famous colleges</a><br>
<a name="3.2.87">Almost in Christendom: shortly, I believe,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.88">His second marriage shall be publish'd, and</a><br>
<a name="3.2.89">Her coronation. Katharine no more</a><br>
<a name="3.2.90">Shall be call'd queen, but princess dowager</a><br>
<a name="3.2.91">And widow to Prince Arthur.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech28"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.92">This same Cranmer's</a><br>
<a name="3.2.93">A worthy fellow, and hath ta'en much pain</a><br>
<a name="3.2.94">In the king's business.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech29"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.95">He has; and we shall see him</a><br>
<a name="3.2.96">For it an archbishop.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech30"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.97">So I hear.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech31"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.98">'Tis so.</a><br>
<a name="3.2.99">The cardinal!</a><br>
<p><i>Enter CARDINAL WOLSEY and CROMWELL</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech32"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.100">                  Observe, observe, he's moody.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech33"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.101">The packet, Cromwell.</a><br>
<a name="3.2.102">Gave't you the king?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech34"><b>CROMWELL</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.103">To his own hand, in's bedchamber.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech35"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.104">Look'd he o' the inside of the paper?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech36"><b>CROMWELL</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.105">Presently</a><br>
<a name="3.2.106">He did unseal them: and the first he view'd,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.107">He did it with a serious mind; a heed</a><br>
<a name="3.2.108">Was in his countenance. You he bade</a><br>
<a name="3.2.109">Attend him here this morning.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech37"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.110">Is he ready</a><br>
<a name="3.2.111">To come abroad?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech38"><b>CROMWELL</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.112">                  I think, by this he is.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech39"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.113">Leave me awhile.</a><br>
<p><i>Exit CROMWELL</i></p>
<p><i>Aside</i></p>
<a name="3.2.114">It shall be to the Duchess of Alencon,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.115">The French king's sister: he shall marry her.</a><br>
<a name="3.2.116">Anne Bullen! No; I'll no Anne Bullens for him:</a><br>
<a name="3.2.117">There's more in't than fair visage. Bullen!</a><br>
<a name="3.2.118">No, we'll no Bullens. Speedily I wish</a><br>
<a name="3.2.119">To hear from Rome. The Marchioness of Pembroke!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech40"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.120">He's discontented.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech41"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.121">                  May be, he hears the king</a><br>
<a name="3.2.122">Does whet his anger to him.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech42"><b>SURREY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.123">Sharp enough,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.124">Lord, for thy justice!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech43"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.125">[Aside]  The late queen's gentlewoman,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.126">a knight's daughter,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.127">To be her mistress' mistress! the queen's queen!</a><br>
<a name="3.2.128">This candle burns not clear: 'tis I must snuff it;</a><br>
<a name="3.2.129">Then out it goes. What though I know her virtuous</a><br>
<a name="3.2.130">And well deserving? yet I know her for</a><br>
<a name="3.2.131">A spleeny Lutheran; and not wholesome to</a><br>
<a name="3.2.132">Our cause, that she should lie i' the bosom of</a><br>
<a name="3.2.133">Our hard-ruled king. Again, there is sprung up</a><br>
<a name="3.2.134">An heretic, an arch one, Cranmer; one</a><br>
<a name="3.2.135">Hath crawl'd into the favour of the king,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.136">And is his oracle.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech44"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.137">                  He is vex'd at something.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech45"><b>SURREY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.138">I would 'twere something that would fret the string,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.139">The master-cord on's heart!</a><br>
<p><i>Enter KING HENRY VIII, reading of a schedule, and LOVELL</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech46"><b>SUFFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.140">The king, the king!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech47"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.141">What piles of wealth hath he accumulated</a><br>
<a name="3.2.142">To his own portion! and what expense by the hour</a><br>
<a name="3.2.143">Seems to flow from him! How, i' the name of thrift,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.144">Does he rake this together! Now, my lords,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.145">Saw you the cardinal?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech48"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.146">My lord, we have</a><br>
<a name="3.2.147">Stood here observing him: some strange commotion</a><br>
<a name="3.2.148">Is in his brain: he bites his lip, and starts;</a><br>
<a name="3.2.149">Stops on a sudden, looks upon the ground,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.150">Then lays his finger on his temple, straight</a><br>
<a name="3.2.151">Springs out into fast gait; then stops again,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.152">Strikes his breast hard, and anon he casts</a><br>
<a name="3.2.153">His eye against the moon: in most strange postures</a><br>
<a name="3.2.154">We have seen him set himself.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech49"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.155">It may well be;</a><br>
<a name="3.2.156">There is a mutiny in's mind. This morning</a><br>
<a name="3.2.157">Papers of state he sent me to peruse,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.158">As I required: and wot you what I found</a><br>
<a name="3.2.159">There,--on my conscience, put unwittingly?</a><br>
<a name="3.2.160">Forsooth, an inventory, thus importing;</a><br>
<a name="3.2.161">The several parcels of his plate, his treasure,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.162">Rich stuffs, and ornaments of household; which</a><br>
<a name="3.2.163">I find at such proud rate, that it out-speaks</a><br>
<a name="3.2.164">Possession of a subject.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech50"><b>NORFOLK</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.165">It's heaven's will:</a><br>
<a name="3.2.166">Some spirit put this paper in the packet,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.167">To bless your eye withal.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech51"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.168">If we did think</a><br>
<a name="3.2.169">His contemplation were above the earth,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.170">And fix'd on spiritual object, he should still</a><br>
<a name="3.2.171">Dwell in his musings: but I am afraid</a><br>
<a name="3.2.172">His thinkings are below the moon, not worth</a><br>
<a name="3.2.173">His serious considering.</a><br>
<p><i>King HENRY VIII takes his seat; whispers LOVELL, who goes to CARDINAL WOLSEY</i></p>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech52"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.174">Heaven forgive me!</a><br>
<a name="3.2.175">Ever God bless your highness!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech53"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.176">Good my lord,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.177">You are full of heavenly stuff, and bear the inventory</a><br>
<a name="3.2.178">Of your best graces in your mind; the which</a><br>
<a name="3.2.179">You were now running o'er: you have scarce time</a><br>
<a name="3.2.180">To steal from spiritual leisure a brief span</a><br>
<a name="3.2.181">To keep your earthly audit: sure, in that</a><br>
<a name="3.2.182">I deem you an ill husband, and am glad</a><br>
<a name="3.2.183">To have you therein my companion.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech54"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.184">Sir,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.185">For holy offices I have a time; a time</a><br>
<a name="3.2.186">To think upon the part of business which</a><br>
<a name="3.2.187">I bear i' the state; and nature does require</a><br>
<a name="3.2.188">Her times of preservation, which perforce</a><br>
<a name="3.2.189">I, her frail son, amongst my brethren mortal,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.190">Must give my tendence to.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech55"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.191">You have said well.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech56"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.192">And ever may your highness yoke together,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.193">As I will lend you cause, my doing well</a><br>
<a name="3.2.194">With my well saying!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech57"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.195">'Tis well said again;</a><br>
<a name="3.2.196">And 'tis a kind of good deed to say well:</a><br>
<a name="3.2.197">And yet words are no deeds. My father loved you:</a><br>
<a name="3.2.198">His said he did; and with his deed did crown</a><br>
<a name="3.2.199">His word upon you. Since I had my office,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.200">I have kept you next my heart; have not alone</a><br>
<a name="3.2.201">Employ'd you where high profits might come home,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.202">But pared my present havings, to bestow</a><br>
<a name="3.2.203">My bounties upon you.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech58"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.204">[Aside]             What should this mean?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech59"><b>SURREY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.205">[Aside]  The Lord increase this business!</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech60"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.206">Have I not made you,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.207">The prime man of the state? I pray you, tell me,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.208">If what I now pronounce you have found true:</a><br>
<a name="3.2.209">And, if you may confess it, say withal,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.210">If you are bound to us or no. What say you?</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech61"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.211">My sovereign, I confess your royal graces,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.212">Shower'd on me daily, have been more than could</a><br>
<a name="3.2.213">My studied purposes requite; which went</a><br>
<a name="3.2.214">Beyond all man's endeavours: my endeavours</a><br>
<a name="3.2.215">Have ever come too short of my desires,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.216">Yet filed with my abilities: mine own ends</a><br>
<a name="3.2.217">Have been mine so that evermore they pointed</a><br>
<a name="3.2.218">To the good of your most sacred person and</a><br>
<a name="3.2.219">The profit of the state. For your great graces</a><br>
<a name="3.2.220">Heap'd upon me, poor undeserver, I</a><br>
<a name="3.2.221">Can nothing render but allegiant thanks,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.222">My prayers to heaven for you, my loyalty,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.223">Which ever has and ever shall be growing,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.224">Till death, that winter, kill it.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech62"><b>KING HENRY VIII</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.225">Fairly answer'd;</a><br>
<a name="3.2.226">A loyal and obedient subject is</a><br>
<a name="3.2.227">Therein illustrated: the honour of it</a><br>
<a name="3.2.228">Does pay the act of it; as, i' the contrary,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.229">The foulness is the punishment. I presume</a><br>
<a name="3.2.230">That, as my hand has open'd bounty to you,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.231">My heart dropp'd love, my power rain'd honour, more</a><br>
<a name="3.2.232">On you than any; so your hand and heart,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.233">Your brain, and every function of your power,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.234">Should, notwithstanding that your bond of duty,</a><br>
<a name="3.2.235">As 'twere in love's particular, be more</a><br>
<a name="3.2.236">To me, your friend, than any.</a><br>
</blockquote>

<a name="speech63"><b>CARDINAL WOLSEY</b></a>
<blockquote>
<a name="3.2.237">I do profess</a><br>
<a name="3.2.238">That for your highness' good I ever labour'd</a><br>
